## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# big-code-kafka-bug-001: Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition

## Task

Investigate a bug in the Apache Kafka producer where a race condition in the `BufferPool` memory management causes messages to silently appear on the wrong topic. Trace the execution path from the producer's `send()` method through batch accumulation, buffer allocation, and network transmission to identify how buffer reuse can corrupt in-flight produce requests.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/kafka--be816b82 (mirror of apache/kafka) (Java, ~800K LOC)
- **Category**: Bug Investigation
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Entry Point**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — `sendProducerData()` and `failBatch()` methods

## Symptom

Users of the Kafka producer with non-zero `linger.ms` observe that messages published to topic A occasionally appear on topic B instead. The corruption is rare but occurs in bursts, typically during broker restarts or network disruptions. The CRC checksum on the records passes because it covers only key/value/headers, not the topic name. The produce request header (containing topic/partition) is serialized separately from the message payload.

The bug is a race condition: when an in-flight `ProducerBatch` expires or its broker disconnects, the batch's pooled `ByteBuffer` is returned to the `BufferPool` and immediately reused by a new batch — while the original batch's request is still being written to the network by the `Sender` thread.

## Requirements

1. Starting from the entry point, trace the execution path to the root cause
2. Identify the specific file(s) and line(s) where the bug originates
3. Explain WHY the bug occurs (not just WHERE) — focus on the buffer lifecycle
4. Propose a fix with specific code changes

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — examined for [reason]
- path/to/file2.ext — examined for [reason]
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Symptom observed in: path/to/symptom.ext
2. Called from: path/to/caller.ext (function name)
3. Bug triggered by: path/to/buggy.ext (function name, line ~N)
...

## Root Cause
- **File**: path/to/root_cause.ext
- **Function**: function_name()
- **Line**: ~N
- **Explanation**: [Why this code is buggy]

## Proposed Fix
```diff
- buggy code
+ fixed code
```

## Analysis
[Detailed trace from symptom to root cause, explaining each step]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- Root cause identification: Did you find the correct file(s) where the bug originates?
- Call chain accuracy: Did you trace the correct path from symptom to root cause?
- Fix quality: Is the proposed fix correct and minimal?

# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition Analysis

## Files Examined
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — Entry point for producer batch sending and failure handling
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — Batch accumulation and buffer deallocation
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` — Memory buffer management and reuse
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — Individual batch structure holding buffer references
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/NetworkClient.java` — Network request serialization and in-flight tracking

## Dependency Chain

1. **Entry point**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357)
   - Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395
   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396
   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends

2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)
   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`
   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`
   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616
120-assistanttext-
Perfect! I have completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition. Here's a summary:

## Summary

I've traced the race condition bug in Apache Kafka's producer that causes messages to silently appear on the wrong topic. The analysis is saved in `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

### Root Cause Found

**Location**: `Sender.java`, line 835 in `failBatch()` method

The bug occurs because:
1. When a `ProducerBatch` is sent, its ByteBuffer is held by a `Send` object in the NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests`
2. If the batch expires before the response arrives, `failBatch()` immediately deallocates the buffer
3. The buffer is returned to the pool and made available for reuse
4. A new batch allocates the same buffer and writes to it
5. Meanwhile, the original `Send` object is still writing the (now corrupted) buffer to the socket
6. The result: messages from the new batch are sent with the wrong topic/partition metadata

### The Fix

Two changes to `Sender.java`:

**1. `failBatch()` (line 835)**: Don't deallocate immediately
```diff
- maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);
+ maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);  // Just remove tracking, don't deallocate
```

**2. `completeBatch()` (line 744-752)**: Deallocate when response arrives
```diff
if (batch.complete(response.baseOffset, response.logAppendTime)) {
    maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);
- }
+ } else if (batch.isDone()) {
+     // Batch already failed by failBatch, but response just arrived
+     // Now it's safe to deallocate since request is no longer in-flight
+     maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);
+ }
```

This ensures buffers remain valid while the network layer is using them, preventing the corruption race condition.

  "content": "# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` \u2014 Entry point for producer batch sending and failure handling\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` \u2014 Batch accumulation and buffer deallocation\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` \u2014 Memory buffer management and reuse\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` \u2014 Individual batch structure holding buffer references\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/NetworkClient.java` \u2014 Network request serialization and in-flight tracking\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Entry point**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n   - Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395\n   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396\n   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends\n\n2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)\n   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`\n   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`\n   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616\n   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`\n\n3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)\n   - Calls `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` which iterates inFlightBatches\n   - Removes expired batches from inFlightBatches at line 191\n\n4. **Batch failure handling**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 817)\n   - Calls `batch.completeExceptionally()` at line 825\n   - Calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 835\n\n5. **Buffer deallocation**: `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` (line 1027)\n   - Calls `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity())` at line 1032\n\n6. **Buffer reuse**: `BufferPool.deallocate()` (line 260)\n   - Clears buffer at line 264: `buffer.clear()`\n   - Adds to free list at line 265: `this.free.add(buffer)`\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817) and `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n**Line**: ~835 (in failBatch) and ~418 (calling failBatch)\n\n### Why the Bug Occurs\n\nThe race condition happens because:\n\n1. **Request sent asynchronously**: When `sendProduceRequest()` calls `client.send()` at line 914, the request is NOT immediately written to the socket. Instead, it's queued in the NetworkClient and will be serialized and sent by the network I/O thread when the socket is ready.\n\n2. **Request holds buffer reference**: The NetworkClient's `doSend()` method (line 608) calls `request.toSend(header)` which creates a `Send` object containing references to the batch's ByteBuffer. This Send object is held in `inFlightRequests` (line 616).\n\n3. **Expired batch deallocates buffer immediately**: When `Sender.sendProducerData()` checks for expired in-flight batches (line 406-407):\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` removes the batch from `inFlightBatches` (line 191)\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - Inside `failBatch()`, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called at line 835\n   - This calls `accumulator.deallocate()` which returns the buffer to the BufferPool (line 1032)\n   - The buffer is cleared and added to the free list (line 265)\n\n4. **Buffer reused while still in-flight**: The buffer is now available in the free list, even though the Send object in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` still holds a reference to it and may still be writing it to the socket.\n\n5. **Corruption occurs**: A new batch allocates the same buffer from the free list (via `accumulator.allocate()`), writes its data to it, and modifies its contents. Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n\n### The Core Issue\n\nThe key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n```\n\nThis line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n\n1. Mark the batch as failed\n2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n\n### Implementation\n\n**Modification to Sender.java, failBatch() method (line 817-836)**:\n\n```diff\nprivate void failBatch(\n    ProducerBatch batch,\n    RuntimeException topLevelException,\n    Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n    boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n) {\n    this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n\n    if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n        if (transactionManager != null) {\n            try {\n                transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n            } catch (Exception e) {\n                log.debug(\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\", e);\n            }\n        }\n-       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+       // For in-flight batches, don't deallocate the buffer here.\n+       // The buffer is still referenced by the Send object in the NetworkClient.\n+       // We'll deallocate it when the response is received (in completeBatch)\n+       // or when the network connection closes.\n+       maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis change ensures that:\n- The batch is still tracked until its request completes\n- The buffer stays allocated and under the control of the in-flight Send object\n- Deallocation happens safely in `completeBatch()` after the response is received\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. In NetworkClient, request is built and Send object is created (line 608)\n5. Send object is queued to selector, awaiting network I/O (line 617)\n6. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. Messages intended for topic A have topic B data, or vice versa\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum in Kafka only covers the record key/value/headers, not the topic/partition metadata. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately). When the buffer is reused mid-write, the corruption affects the message payload, but since the CRC was already embedded when the batch was created, it doesn't detect the corruption if only the buffer contents were overwritten after CRC calculation.\n\n### Impact\n\nThis bug manifests as messages silently appearing on wrong topics, especially during:\n- Network disruptions or broker restarts (causing timeouts)\n- High latency scenarios with lingering enabled (`linger.ms > 0`)\n- Burst traffic that triggers batch expiration\n",

  "originalFile": "# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` \u2014 Entry point for producer batch sending and failure handling\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` \u2014 Batch accumulation and buffer deallocation\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` \u2014 Memory buffer management and reuse\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` \u2014 Individual batch structure holding buffer references\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/NetworkClient.java` \u2014 Network request serialization and in-flight tracking\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Entry point**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n   - Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395\n   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396\n   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends\n\n2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)\n   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`\n   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`\n   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616\n   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`\n\n3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)\n   - Calls `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` which iterates inFlightBatches\n   - Removes expired batches from inFlightBatches at line 191\n\n4. **Batch failure handling**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 817)\n   - Calls `batch.completeExceptionally()` at line 825\n   - Calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 835\n\n5. **Buffer deallocation**: `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` (line 1027)\n   - Calls `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity())` at line 1032\n\n6. **Buffer reuse**: `BufferPool.deallocate()` (line 260)\n   - Clears buffer at line 264: `buffer.clear()`\n   - Adds to free list at line 265: `this.free.add(buffer)`\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817) and `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n**Line**: ~835 (in failBatch) and ~418 (calling failBatch)\n\n### Why the Bug Occurs\n\nThe race condition happens because:\n\n1. **Request sent asynchronously**: When `sendProduceRequest()` calls `client.send()` at line 914, the request is NOT immediately written to the socket. Instead, it's queued in the NetworkClient and will be serialized and sent by the network I/O thread when the socket is ready.\n\n2. **Request holds buffer reference**: The NetworkClient's `doSend()` method (line 608) calls `request.toSend(header)` which creates a `Send` object containing references to the batch's ByteBuffer. This Send object is held in `inFlightRequests` (line 616).\n\n3. **Expired batch deallocates buffer immediately**: When `Sender.sendProducerData()` checks for expired in-flight batches (line 406-407):\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` removes the batch from `inFlightBatches` (line 191)\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - Inside `failBatch()`, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called at line 835\n   - This calls `accumulator.deallocate()` which returns the buffer to the BufferPool (line 1032)\n   - The buffer is cleared and added to the free list (line 265)\n\n4. **Buffer reused while still in-flight**: The buffer is now available in the free list, even though the Send object in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` still holds a reference to it and may still be writing it to the socket.\n\n5. **Corruption occurs**: A new batch allocates the same buffer from the free list (via `accumulator.allocate()`), writes its data to it, and modifies its contents. Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n\n### The Core Issue\n\nThe key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n```\n\nThis line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n\n1. Mark the batch as failed\n2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n\n### Implementation\n\n**Modification to Sender.java, failBatch() method (line 817-836)**:\n\n```diff\nprivate void failBatch(\n    ProducerBatch batch,\n    RuntimeException topLevelException,\n    Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n    boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n) {\n    this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n\n    if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n        if (transactionManager != null) {\n            try {\n                transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n            } catch (Exception e) {\n                log.debug(\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\", e);\n            }\n        }\n-       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+       // For in-flight batches, don't deallocate the buffer here.\n+       // The buffer is still referenced by the Send object in the NetworkClient.\n+       // We'll deallocate it when the response is received (in completeBatch)\n+       // or when the network connection closes.\n+       maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis change ensures that:\n- The batch is still tracked until its request completes\n- The buffer stays allocated and under the control of the in-flight Send object\n- Deallocation happens safely in `completeBatch()` after the response is received\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. In NetworkClient, request is built and Send object is created (line 608)\n5. Send object is queued to selector, awaiting network I/O (line 617)\n6. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately).   "new_string": "**Key insight**: The buffer deallocation should happen at the END of the batch lifecycle (when response is received), not when the batch expires. The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first.\n\n### Why This Fix is Safe\n\nThe fix is safe because:\n\n1. **No double deallocation**: When a response arrives in `completeBatch()`, it calls `batch.complete()` which checks the batch's final state (line 218). If the batch was already marked as failed by `failBatch()`, then `complete()` returns false and `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is NOT called (line 750).\n\n2. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (still in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests`) is writing to the socket.\n\n3. **Eventual cleanup**: When the response finally arrives or the connection closes:\n   - If response arrives: `completeBatch()` handles deallocation (though skipped due to final state check)\n   - If connection closes: The NetworkClient will clean up in-flight requests\n\n4. **Matches design intent**: Buffer pools are meant to manage buffer lifecycle. The accumulator should only deallocate when the batch lifecycle is truly complete (response received or connection error), not at expiration time.",

  "originalFile": "# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` \u2014 Entry point for producer batch sending and failure handling\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` \u2014 Batch accumulation and buffer deallocation\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` \u2014 Memory buffer management and reuse\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` \u2014 Individual batch structure holding buffer references\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/NetworkClient.java` \u2014 Network request serialization and in-flight tracking\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Entry point**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n   - Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395\n   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396\n   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends\n\n2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)\n   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`\n   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`\n   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616\n   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`\n\n3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)\n   - Calls `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` which iterates inFlightBatches\n   - Removes expired batches from inFlightBatches at line 191\n\n4. **Batch failure handling**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 817)\n   - Calls `batch.completeExceptionally()` at line 825\n   - Calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 835\n\n5. **Buffer deallocation**: `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` (line 1027)\n   - Calls `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity())` at line 1032\n\n6. **Buffer reuse**: `BufferPool.deallocate()` (line 260)\n   - Clears buffer at line 264: `buffer.clear()`\n   - Adds to free list at line 265: `this.free.add(buffer)`\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817) and `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n**Line**: ~835 (in failBatch) and ~418 (calling failBatch)\n\n### Why the Bug Occurs\n\nThe race condition happens because:\n\n1. **Request sent asynchronously**: When `sendProduceRequest()` calls `client.send()` at line 914, the request is NOT immediately written to the socket. Instead, it's queued in the NetworkClient and will be serialized and sent by the network I/O thread when the socket is ready.\n\n2. **Request holds buffer reference**: The NetworkClient's `doSend()` method (line 608) calls `request.toSend(header)` which creates a `Send` object containing references to the batch's ByteBuffer. This Send object is held in `inFlightRequests` (line 616).\n\n3. **Expired batch deallocates buffer immediately**: When `Sender.sendProducerData()` checks for expired in-flight batches (line 406-407):\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` removes the batch from `inFlightBatches` (line 191)\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - Inside `failBatch()`, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called at line 835\n   - This calls `accumulator.deallocate()` which returns the buffer to the BufferPool (line 1032)\n   - The buffer is cleared and added to the free list (line 265)\n\n4. **Buffer reused while still in-flight**: The buffer is now available in the free list, even though the Send object in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` still holds a reference to it and may still be writing it to the socket.\n\n5. **Corruption occurs**: A new batch allocates the same buffer from the free list (via `accumulator.allocate()`), writes its data to it, and modifies its contents. Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n\n### The Core Issue\n\nThe key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n```\n\nThis line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n\n1. Mark the batch as failed\n2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n\n### Implementation\n\nThe core issue is at **line 835 in Sender.java**, within the `failBatch()` method:\n\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // UNSAFE for in-flight batches\n```\n\nThis unconditionally deallocates the buffer, but the batch's request might still be queued in the NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` (line 616 in NetworkClient.doSend()).\n\n**Solution: Don't deallocate buffers in failBatch() - let completeBatch() handle it**\n\nThe fix requires modifying `failBatch()` to avoid deallocating buffers for batches that are still in-flight. Instead of:\n\n```diff\n- maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n```\n\nWe should:\n\n```diff\n+ // Don't deallocate buffer here - it's still in-flight in NetworkClient.\n+ // The buffer will be deallocated in completeBatch() when response arrives.\n+ // If response never arrives, the connection closure will clean it up.\n+ maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n```\n\nThis change ensures that:\n1. **The batch is removed from tracking** via `maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches()` (line 173)\n2. **The buffer remains allocated** while in-flight\n3. **Safe deallocation happens in completeBatch()** (line 750) when the response is received\n4. **No corruption occurs** because the Send object always has valid buffer contents\n\n**Key insight**: The buffer deallocation should happen at the END of the batch lifecycle (when response is received), not when the batch expires. The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. Messages intended for topic A have topic B data, or vice versa\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum in Kafka only covers the record key/value/headers, not the topic/partition metadata. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately). When the buffer is reused mid-write, the corruption affects the message payload, but since the CRC was already embedded when the batch was created, it doesn't detect the corruption if only the buffer contents were overwritten after CRC calculation.\n\n### Impact\n\nThis bug manifests as messages silently appearing on wrong topics, especially during:\n- Network disruptions or broker restarts (causing timeouts)\n- High latency scenarios with lingering enabled (`linger.ms > 0`)\n- Burst traffic that triggers batch expiration\n",

Clears buffer at line 264: `buffer.clear()`\n   - Adds to free list at line 265: `this.free.add(buffer)`\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817) and `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n**Line**: ~835 (in failBatch) and ~418 (calling failBatch)\n\n### Why the Bug Occurs\n\nThe race condition happens because:\n\n1. **Request sent asynchronously**: When `sendProduceRequest()` calls `client.send()` at line 914, the request is NOT immediately written to the socket. Instead, it's queued in the NetworkClient and will be serialized and sent by the network I/O thread when the socket is ready.\n\n2. **Request holds buffer reference**: The NetworkClient's `doSend()` method (line 608) calls `request.toSend(header)` which creates a `Send` object containing references to the batch's ByteBuffer. This Send object is held in `inFlightRequests` (line 616).\n\n3. **Expired batch deallocates buffer immediately**: When `Sender.sendProducerData()` checks for expired in-flight batches (line 406-407):\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` removes the batch from `inFlightBatches` (line 191)\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - Inside `failBatch()`, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called at line 835\n   - This calls `accumulator.deallocate()` which returns the buffer to the BufferPool (line 1032)\n   - The buffer is cleared and added to the free list (line 265)\n\n4. **Buffer reused while still in-flight**: The buffer is now available in the free list, even though the Send object in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` still holds a reference to it and may still be writing it to the socket.\n\n5. **Corruption occurs**: A new batch allocates the same buffer from the free list (via `accumulator.allocate()`), writes its data to it, and modifies its contents. Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n\n### The Core Issue\n\nThe key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n```\n\nThis line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n\n1. Mark the batch as failed\n2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n\n### Implementation\n\nThe core issue is at **line 835 in Sender.java**, within the `failBatch()` method:\n\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // UNSAFE for in-flight batches\n```\n\nThis unconditionally deallocates the buffer, but the batch's request might still be queued in the NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` (line 616 in NetworkClient.doSend()).\n\n**Solution: Don't deallocate buffers in failBatch() - let completeBatch() handle it**\n\nThe fix requires modifying `failBatch()` to avoid deallocating buffers for batches that are still in-flight. Instead of:\n\n```diff\n- maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n```\n\nWe should:\n\n```diff\n+ // Don't deallocate buffer here - it's still in-flight in NetworkClient.\n+ // The buffer will be deallocated in completeBatch() when response arrives.\n+ // If response never arrives, the connection closure will clean it up.\n+ maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n```\n\nThis change ensures that:\n1. **The batch is removed from tracking** via `maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches()` (line 173)\n2. **The buffer remains allocated** while in-flight\n3. **Safe deallocation happens in completeBatch()** (line 750) when the response is received\n4. **No corruption occurs** because the Send object always has valid buffer contents\n\n**Key insight**: The buffer deallocation should happen at the END of the batch lifecycle (when response is received), not when the batch expires. The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first.\n\n### Why This Fix is Safe\n\nThe fix is safe because:\n\n1. **No double deallocation**: When a response arrives in `completeBatch()`, it calls `batch.complete()` which checks the batch's final state (line 218). If the batch was already marked as failed by `failBatch()`, then `complete()` returns false and `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is NOT called (line 750).\n\n2. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (still in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests`) is writing to the socket.\n\n3. **Eventual cleanup**: When the response finally arrives or the connection closes:\n   - If response arrives: `completeBatch()` handles deallocation (though skipped due to final state check)\n   - If connection closes: The NetworkClient will clean up in-flight requests\n\n4. **Matches design intent**: Buffer pools are meant to manage buffer lifecycle. The accumulator should only deallocate when the batch lifecycle is truly complete (response received or connection error), not at expiration time.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. In NetworkClient, request is built and Send object is created (line 608)\n5. Send object is queued to selector, awaiting network I/O (line 617)\n6. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. Messages intended for topic A have topic B data, or vice versa\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum in Kafka only covers the record key/value/headers, not the topic/partition metadata. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately). When the buffer is reused mid-write, the corruption affects the message payload, but since the CRC was already embedded when the batch was created, it doesn't detect the corruption if only the buffer contents were overwritten after CRC calculation.\n\n### Impact\n\nThis bug manifests as messages silently appearing on wrong topics, especially during:\n- Network disruptions or broker restarts (causing timeouts)\n- High latency scenarios with lingering enabled (`linger.ms > 0`)\n- Burst traffic that triggers batch expiration\n",

Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395\n   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396\n   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends\n\n2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)\n   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`\n   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`\n   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616\n   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`\n\n3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)\n   - Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n\n### The Core Issue\n\nThe key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n```\n\nThis line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n\n1. Mark the batch as failed\n2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3.  // UNSAFE - buffer still in-flight!\n```\n\nThis should be changed to:\n\n```diff\n- maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+ // Don't deallocate buffer here - the request is still queued in NetworkClient.\n+ // The buffer reference is held by the Send object in inFlightRequests.\n+ // We'll deallocate when the response arrives (in completeBatch) or connection closes.\n+ maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n```\n\n**Change 2: completeBatch() - Deallocate even if batch already failed (line 744-752)**\n\nThe response handler must deallocate buffers for batches that were already marked failed:\n\n```diff\nprivate void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {\n    if (transactionManager != null) {\n        transactionManager.handleCompletedBatch(batch, response);\n    }\n\n    if (batch.complete(response.baseOffset, response.logAppendTime)) {\n        maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n-   }\n+   } else if (batch.isDone()) {\n+       // Batch already completed (failed by failBatch due to expiration)\n+       // Still need to deallocate the buffer now that request is no longer in-flight\n+       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+   }\n}\n```\n\nTogether, these changes ensure:\n1. **Expired batches are marked failed immediately** (user gets error notification via `completeExceptionally()`)\n2. **Buffers remain valid until network write completes** (Send object can safely serialize the batch)\n3. **Safe deallocation happens after request is done** (when response arrives or connection closes)\n4. **No corruption occurs** because the batch's buffer is never reused while in-flight\n\n### Why This Fix is Safe\n\nThe fix is safe because:\n\n1. **No double deallocation**: When a response arrives in `completeBatch()`, it calls `batch.complete()` which checks the batch's final state (line 218). If the batch was already marked as failed by `failBatch()`, then `complete()` returns false and `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is NOT called (line 750).\n\n2. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (still in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests`) is writing to the socket.\n\n3. **Eventual cleanup**: When the response finally arrives or the connection closes:\n   - If response arrives: `completeBatch()` handles deallocation (though skipped due to final state check)\n   - If connection closes: The NetworkClient will clean up in-flight requests\n\n4. **Matches design intent**: Buffer pools are meant to manage buffer lifecycle. The accumulator should only deallocate when the batch lifecycle is truly complete (response received or connection error), not at expiration time.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395\n   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396\n   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends\n\n2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)\n   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`\n   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`\n   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616\n   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`\n\n3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)\n   - Calls `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` which iterates inFlightBatches\n   - Removes expired batches from inFlightBatches at line 191\n\n4. **Batch failure handling**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 817)\n   - Calls `batch.completeExceptionally()` at line 825\n   - Calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 835\n\n5. **Buffer deallocation**: `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` (line 1027)\n   - Calls `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity())` at line 1032\n\n6. **Buffer reuse**: `BufferPool.deallocate()` (line 260)\n   - Clears buffer at line 264: `buffer.clear()`\n   - Adds to free list at line 265: `this.free.add(buffer)`\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817) and `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n**Line**: ~835 (in failBatch) and ~418 (calling failBatch)\n\n### Why the Bug Occurs\n\nThe race condition happens because:\n\n1. **Request sent asynchronously**: When `sendProduceRequest()` calls `client.send()` at line 914, the request is NOT immediately written to the socket. Instead, it's queued in the NetworkClient and will be serialized and sent by the network I/O thread when the socket is ready.\n\n2. **Request holds buffer reference**: The NetworkClient's `doSend()` method (line 608) calls `request.toSend(header)` which creates a `Send` object containing references to the batch's ByteBuffer. This Send object is held in `inFlightRequests` (line 616).\n\n3. **Expired batch deallocates buffer immediately**: When `Sender.sendProducerData()` checks for expired in-flight batches (line 406-407):\n   - `getExpiredInflightBatches()` removes the batch from `inFlightBatches` (line 191)\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - Inside `failBatch()`, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called at line 835\n   - This calls `accumulator.deallocate()` which returns the buffer to the BufferPool (line 1032)\n   - The buffer is cleared and added to the free list (line 265)\n\n4. **Buffer reused while still in-flight**: The buffer is now available in the free list, even though the Send object in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` still holds a reference to it and may still be writing it to the socket.\n\n5. **Corruption occurs**: A new batch allocates the same buffer from the free list (via `accumulator.allocate()`), writes its data to it, and modifies its contents. Meanwhile, the original Send object is still writing to the socket, but the buffer now contains corrupted data from the new batch.\n\n### The Core Issue\n\nThe key vulnerability is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // Called in failBatch()\n```\n\nThis line deallocates the buffer for a batch that is still in-flight in the NetworkClient. The batch's request may still be queued in the selector, waiting to be written to the socket, or currently being written. The Send object holds a reference to the ByteBuffer, not a copy of it.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix requires separating buffer deallocation from batch failure handling. When a batch expires while in-flight, we should NOT deallocate its buffer immediately. Instead, we should:\n\n1. Mark the batch as failed\n2. Let the buffer remain allocated and referenced by the in-flight Send object\n3. Deallocate the buffer only when the response is received (in `completeBatch()`) or when the network connection is definitively closed\n\n### Implementation\n\nThe fix requires TWO changes to Sender.java to prevent deallocating buffers while they're still in-flight:\n\n**Change 1: failBatch() - Don't deallocate immediately (line 817-836)**\n\nThe core issue is at **line 835 in Sender.java**:\n\n```java\nmaybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // UNSAFE - buffer still in-flight!\n```\n\nThis should be changed to:\n\n```diff\n- maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+ // Don't deallocate buffer here - the request is still queued in NetworkClient.\n+ // The buffer reference is held by the Send object in inFlightRequests.\n+ // We'll deallocate when the response arrives (in completeBatch) or connection closes.\n+ maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n```\n\n**Change 2: completeBatch() - Deallocate even if batch already failed (line 744-752)**\n\nThe response handler must deallocate buffers for batches that were already marked failed:\n\n```diff\nprivate void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {\n    if (transactionManager != null) {\n        transactionManager.handleCompletedBatch(batch, response);\n    }\n\n    if (batch.complete(response.baseOffset, response.logAppendTime)) {\n        maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n-   }\n+   } else if (batch.isDone()) {\n+       // Batch already completed (failed by failBatch due to expiration)\n+       // Still need to deallocate the buffer now that request is no longer in-flight\n+       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+   }\n}\n```\n\nTogether, these changes ensure:\n1. **Expired batches are marked failed immediately** (user gets error notification via `completeExceptionally()`)\n2. **Buffers remain valid until network write completes** (Send object can safely serialize the batch)\n3. **Safe deallocation happens after request is done** (when response arrives or connection closes)\n4. **No corruption occurs** because the batch's buffer is never reused while in-flight\n\n### Why This Fix is Safe\n\nThe fix is safe because:\n\n1. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` at line 616) is writing to the socket. New batches cannot reuse the buffer until the network layer releases it.\n\n2. **No double deallocation**: The new `else if` condition in `completeBatch()` ensures we only deallocate once:\n   - Successful response: `batch.complete()` returns true and deallocates\n   - Failed response after batch still in-flight: `batch.complete()` returns false, but `batch.isDone()` is true, so we deallocate\n   - No path deallocates twice\n\n3. **Immediate error notification**: Users still get immediate timeout exceptions via `batch.completeExceptionally()` in `failBatch()`, so the error is reported right away even though deallocation is delayed.\n\n4. **Eventual cleanup guaranteed**:\n   - Normal case: Response arrives \u2192 `completeBatch()` deallocates\n   - Network error: Connection closes \u2192 NetworkClient discards Send object \u2192 buffer eventually cleaned up\n   - Connection timeout: Request times out \u2192 NetworkClient removes from `inFlightRequests` \u2192 can be deallocated\n\n5. **Handles all failBatch() call sites**:\n   - Expired batches (line 418): Buffer stays alive until response or timeout\n   - Error responses (line 720): Buffer already no longer in-flight, `completeBatch()` handles it\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path to Race Condition\n\n1. Producer calls `Sender.run()` which calls `runOnce()`\n2. `runOnce()` calls `sendProducerData()` at line 339\n3. Batches are drained and sent via `sendProduceRequest()` (lines 395, 442)\n4. In NetworkClient, request is built and Send object is created (line 608)\n5. Send object is queued to selector, awaiting network I/O (line 617)\n6. Meanwhile, in the next `sendProducerData()` call, batch expiration is checked (line 406)\n7. Expired batch is found and removed from inFlightBatches (line 191)\n8. `failBatch()` is called, which deallocates the buffer (line 835)\n9. Buffer is returned to pool and added to free list (line 265)\n10. New batch allocates same buffer, writes to it\n11. Original Send object writes corrupted data to socket\n12. Messages intended for topic A have topic B data, or vice versa\n\n### Why CRC Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum in Kafka only covers the record key/value/headers, not the topic/partition metadata. The partition information is in the ProduceRequest header (serialized separately). When the buffer is reused mid-write, the corruption affects the message payload, but since the CRC was already embedded when the batch was created, it doesn't detect the corruption if only the buffer contents were overwritten after CRC calculation.\n\n### Impact\n\nThis bug manifests as messages silently appearing on wrong topics, especially during:\n- Network disruptions or broker restarts (causing timeouts)\n- High latency scenarios with lingering enabled (`linger.ms > 0`)\n- Burst traffic that triggers batch expiration\n",

# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition Analysis

## Files Examined
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — Entry point for producer batch sending and failure handling
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — Batch accumulation and buffer deallocation
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` — Memory buffer management and reuse
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — Individual batch structure holding buffer references
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/NetworkClient.java` — Network request serialization and in-flight tracking

## Dependency Chain

1. **Entry point**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357)
   - Drains ready batches from accumulator at line 395
   - Adds them to inFlightBatches at line 396
   - Calls sendProduceRequests() at line 442 to queue network sends

2. **Request serialization**: `NetworkClient.doSend()` (line 551)
   - Builds the request at line 582: `builder.build(version)`
   - Creates Send object at line 608: `request.toSend(header)`
   - Adds Send to inFlightRequests at line 616
   - Queues to selector at line 617: `selector.send(new NetworkSend(...))`

3. **Batch expiration check**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-407)
   - Calls `getExpiredInflightBatches(now)` which iterates inFlightBatches
   - Removes expired batches from inFlightBatches at line 191

4. **Batch failure handling**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 817)
   - Calls `batch.completeExceptionally()` at line 825
   - Calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 835

5. **Buffer deallocation**: `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` (line 1027)
   - Calls `free.deall

Before
### Implementation

**Modification to Sender.java, failBatch() method (line 817-836)**:

```diff
private void failBatch(
    ProducerBatch batch,
    RuntimeException topLevelException,
    Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,
    boolean adjustSequenceNumbers
) {
    this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);

    if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {
        if (transactionManager != null) {
            try {
                transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);
            } catch (Exception e) {
                log.debug("Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch", e);
            }
        }
-       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);
+       // For in-flight batches, don't deallocate the buffer here.
+       // The buffer is still referenced by the Send object in the NetworkClient.
+       // We'll deallocate it when the response is received (in completeBatch)
+       // or when the network connection closes.
+       maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);
    }
}
```

This change ensures that:
- The batch is still tracked until its request completes
- The buffer stays allocated and under the control of the in-flight Send object
- Deallocation happens safely in `completeBatch()` after the response is received
After
### Implementation

The core issue is at **line 835 in Sender.java**, within the `failBatch()` method:

```java
maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // UNSAFE for in-flight batches
```

This unconditionally deallocates the buffer, but the batch's request might still be queued in the NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` (line 616 in NetworkClient.doSend()).

**Solution: Don't deallocate buffers in failBatch() - let completeBatch() handle it**

The fix requires modifying `failBatch()` to avoid deallocating buffers for batches that are still in-flight. Instead of:

```diff
- maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);
```

We should:

```diff
+ // Don't deallocate buffer here - it's still in-flight in NetworkClient.
+ // The buffer will be deallocated in completeBatch() when response arrives.
+ // If response never arrives, the connection closure will clean it up.
+ maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);
```

This change ensures that:
1. **The batch is removed from tracking** via `maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches()` (line 173)
2. **The buffer remains allocated** while in-flight
3. **Safe deallocation happens in completeBatch()** (line 750) when the response is received
4. **No corruption occurs** because the Send object always has valid buffer contents

**Key insight**: The buffer deallocation should happen at the END of the batch lifecycle (when response is received), not when the batch expires. The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first.
3. EDIT /logs/agent/solution.md
Before
**Key insight**: The buffer deallocation should happen at the END of the batch lifecycle (when response is received), not when the batch expires. The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first.
After
**Key insight**: The buffer deallocation should happen at the END of the batch lifecycle (when response is received), not when the batch expires. The expiration just marks it as failed, but the network layer must finish using it first.

### Why This Fix is Safe

The fix is safe because:

1. **No double deallocation**: When a response arrives in `completeBatch()`, it calls `batch.complete()` which checks the batch's final state (line 218). If the batch was already marked as failed by `failBatch()`, then `complete()` returns false and `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is NOT called (line 750).

2. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (still in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests`) is writing to the socket.

3. **Eventual cleanup**: When the response finally arrives or the connection closes:
   - If response arrives: `completeBatch()` handles deallocation (though skipped due to final state check)
   - If connection closes: The NetworkClient will clean up in-flight requests

4. **Matches design intent**: Buffer pools are meant to manage buffer lifecycle. The accumulator should only deallocate when the batch lifecycle is truly complete (response received or connection error), not at expiration time.

The fix requires TWO changes to Sender.java to prevent deallocating buffers while they're still in-flight:

**Change 1: failBatch() - Don't deallocate immediately (line 817-836)**

```java

This should be changed to:

```diff
- maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);
+ // Don't deallocate buffer here - the request is still queued in NetworkClient.
+ // The buffer reference is held by the Send object in inFlightRequests.
+ // We'll deallocate when the response arrives (in completeBatch) or connection closes.
+ maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);
```

**Change 2: completeBatch() - Deallocate even if batch already failed (line 744-752)**

The response handler must deallocate buffers for batches that were already marked failed:

```diff
private void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {
    if (transactionManager != null) {
        transactionManager.handleCompletedBatch(batch, response);
    }

    if (batch.complete(response.baseOffset, response.logAppendTime)) {
        maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);
-   }
+   } else if (batch.isDone()) {
+       // Batch already completed (failed by failBatch due to expiration)
+       // Still need to deallocate the buffer now that request is no longer in-flight
+       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);
+   }
}
```

Together, these changes ensure:
1. **Expired batches are marked failed immediately** (user gets error notification via `completeExceptionally()`)
2. **Buffers remain valid until network write completes** (Send object can safely serialize the batch)

Before
### Why This Fix is Safe

The fix is safe because:

1. **No double deallocation**: When a response arrives in `completeBatch()`, it calls `batch.complete()` which checks the batch's final state (line 218). If the batch was already marked as failed by `failBatch()`, then `complete()` returns false and `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is NOT called (line 750).

2. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (still in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests`) is writing to the socket.

3. **Eventual cleanup**: When the response finally arrives or the connection closes:
   - If response arrives: `completeBatch()` handles deallocation (though skipped due to final state check)
   - If connection closes: The NetworkClient will clean up in-flight requests

4. **Matches design intent**: Buffer pools are meant to manage buffer lifecycle. The accumulator should only deallocate when the batch lifecycle is truly complete (response received or connection error), not at expiration time.
After
### Why This Fix is Safe

The fix is safe because:

1. **Prevents corruption**: By not deallocating in `failBatch()`, the buffer remains valid while the `Send` object (in NetworkClient's `inFlightRequests` at line 616) is writing to the socket. New batches cannot reuse the buffer until the network layer releases it.

2. **No double deallocation**: The new `else if` condition in `completeBatch()` ensures we only deallocate once:
   - Successful response: `batch.complete()` returns true and deallocates
   - Failed response after batch still in-flight: `batch.complete()` returns false, but `batch.isDone()` is true, so we deallocate
   - No path deallocates twice

3. **Immediate error notification**: Users still get immediate timeout exceptions via `batch.completeExceptionally()` in `failBatch()`, so the error is reported right away even though deallocation is delayed.

4. **Eventual cleanup guaranteed**:
   - Normal case: Response arrives → `completeBatch()` deallocates
   - Network error: Connection closes → NetworkClient discards Send object → buffer eventually cleaned up
   - Connection timeout: Request times out → NetworkClient removes from `inFlightRequests` → can be deallocated

5. **Handles all failBatch() call sites**:
   - Expired batches (line 418): Buffer stays alive until response or timeout
   - Error responses (line 720): Buffer already no longer in-flight, `completeBatch()` handles it
